## Management Summary

### Verdict

🔴 Not production-ready. Juice Shop's authentication boundary is structurally compromised: the private key that signs every user session is committed to a public repository, multiple login paths allow credential bypass without brute force, and any user created through the social login flow receives an account password that anyone who knows their email can compute. A connected set of injection, file-handling, and data-exposure weaknesses means that customer credentials, payment records, and internal key material are reachable by unauthenticated internet visitors.

**Risk distribution:** 🔴 Critical: 7 · 🟠 High: 39 · 🟡 Medium: 15 · 🟢 Low: 0 · **Total: 61**


<br/>

**Attack scenarios directly exercisable against the current codebase:**

<blockquote style="border-left: 3px solid #dc2626; background: #fef2f2; padding: 16px 20px; margin: 0;">

- **Admin session without a password** — Any internet user can obtain an administrator session by downloading the signing key committed to the public repository and forging a token offline, or by supplying a crafted value to the login form that short-circuits the credential check — either path yields administrative access without knowing any password. *(🔴 [F-004](#f-004), 🔴 [F-005](#f-005), 🔴 [F-006](#f-006))* — ✓ **end-to-end verified** ([AC-T-005](#ac-t-005), [AC-T-003](#ac-t-003))
- **Account takeover for any social-login user** — A user who signed up via Google receives a local account password derived solely from their email address using a reversible formula; any party who knows the target email can compute that password and log in as the victim through the standard login page. *(🔴 [F-003](#f-003))*
- **Administrator role claimed at self-registration** — The account-creation endpoint accepts extra fields in the registration request body and passes them directly to the database, allowing any new registrant to assign themselves an administrator role or mark their account as staff before their first login. *(🔴 [F-001](#f-001))* — ✓ **end-to-end verified** ([AC-T-003](#ac-t-003))
- **All customer data extracted via product search** — The product search field accepts unvalidated input passed directly to the database without parameterization; an unauthenticated visitor can extract usernames, stored password digests, full payment card numbers, and two-factor authentication secrets in a single crafted request. *(🔴 [F-008](#f-008), 🔴 [F-006](#f-006))*
- **Any customer account readable by another logged-in user** — Delivery addresses, order history, and account profile data for any customer are accessible to any other authenticated user who substitutes a different account identifier in the request, because the server trusts the identifier submitted rather than the identity established at login. *(🔴 [F-007](#f-007))*

</blockquote>

<br/>

Removing the committed signing key, parameterizing every database query, and verifying authorization server-side on each privileged action are the three changes that eliminate the highest-impact attack paths identified in this assessment.

### Architectural Anti-Patterns

The defects below are structural - each spans multiple findings and requires a design change, not a point fix. See **[§7 Security Architecture](#7-security-architecture)** for the per-control detail.

- **SPA without BFF** — The Angular SPA reads the server-issued JWT and writes it to browser localStorage, where it is reachable by any XSS payload on the same origin. No Backend-for-Frontend layer exists to hold the token in an HttpOnly Secure cookie server-side; a point fix on any individual XSS finding does not close this structural exposure.
    - _Affected components:_ [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend
    - _Findings:_ 🟠 [F-023](#f-023) — JWT stored in browser localStorage (`request.interceptor.ts:16`), 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — Persistent XSS enables token theft (`search-result.component.ts:143`)

- **Raw SQL string interpolation** — Multiple route handlers bypass the Sequelize ORM and concatenate user-controlled request fields directly into raw SQL query strings — a pattern present at the login route, the product search route, and potentially other call sites. No parameterized-query discipline is enforced at the data-access layer, so new routes written in the same style inherit the vulnerability.
    - _Affected components:_ [C-02](#c-02) - Authentication and Identity Service, [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend
    - _Findings:_ 🔴 [F-006](#f-006) — SQL injection in login query (`login.ts:34`), 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — SQL injection in product search (`search.ts:23`)

- **Secrets hardcoded in source** — The RSA private key that signs every user session and a BIP-39 wallet mnemonic are committed verbatim in the repository source files. Any party with read access to the repository — including historical forks and CI/CD caches — holds these secrets permanently; rotating them requires both replacing the key material and forcing active sessions to re-authenticate.
    - _Affected components:_ [C-02](#c-02) - Authentication and Identity Service, [C-08](#c-08) - Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface
    - _Findings:_ 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) — Hardcoded RSA JWT signing key (`insecurity.ts:21`), 🔴 [F-037](#f-037) — Hardcoded BIP-39 wallet mnemonic (`checkKeys.ts:10`)

### AI / LLM Exposure

The Socket\.IO chat endpoint embeds a commercial LLM with live coupon-generation tool access reachable by unauthenticated WebSocket callers, concentrating prompt injection, excessive agency, system-prompt disclosure, and unbounded consumption risks on a single public channel. See **[§7 Security Architecture](#7-security-architecture)** for the per-control detail.



- **LLM01 Prompt Injection** — User chat messages reach the LLM context at `routes/chat.ts` without sanitization or an isolation boundary between user-controlled content and the system prompt, allowing an attacker to override the model's operating instructions and direct the coupon-generation tool to issue codes it should refuse. _([C-05](#c-05) — Socket\.IO Real-Time Server)_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-020](#f-020) — LLM prompt injection drives unauthorised coupon tool (`chat.ts:176`)

- **LLM06 Excessive Agency** — The chat agent is granted direct authority to generate real coupon codes with no human-in-the-loop approval, no scope cap, and no secondary authorization check — so a successful prompt-injection payload immediately materializes as usable discount codes without any further access. _([C-05](#c-05) — Socket\.IO Real-Time Server)_
  - ↳ 🔴 [F-045](#f-045) — Excessive LLM agency in coupon generation (`chat.ts:176`)

- **LLM07 System Prompt Leakage** — The system prompt at `routes/chat.ts` includes internal coupon policy that the model can be induced to repeat verbatim through crafted elicitation requests, disclosing business rules and discount thresholds that are not intended to be visible to end users. _([C-05](#c-05) — Socket\.IO Real-Time Server)_
  - ↳ 🟡 [F-056](#f-056) — System prompt leakage of internal coupon policy (`chat.ts:105`)

- **LLM10 Unbounded Consumption** — The WebSocket chat endpoint at `routes/chat.ts` applies no per-session or per-IP rate limit on LLM API calls, allowing an unauthenticated caller to drive unbounded inference costs against the backend API key through rapid message submission. _([C-05](#c-05) — Socket\.IO Real-Time Server)_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-039](#f-039) — Unbounded LLM consumption on chat endpoint (`chat.ts:114`)

### Security Posture & Top Threats

**Figure 1 - Architecture & Top Threats**

Architecture tiers top-to-bottom (External Actors → Client → Application → Data) with the top threats per component. The in-figure legend on the right explains the attack scenarios, severity dots and symbols.

![Figure 1 - Architecture & Top Threats](threat-model-juice-shop-thorough.figure1.svg)

**Figure 2 - Risk Flow: Actor → Tier → Impact**

Heatmap: **actors** (left) → **architecture tiers** (middle, Client → Application → Data) → **impact** (right). Numbered red arrows ①–⑦ are the threats enumerated in the Top Threats table below. Self-registration is open, so the **Authenticated Internet Attacker** tier is one POST away from anonymous - it is shown distinctly because a post-login endpoint is still a different attack surface.

![Figure 2 - Risk Flow: Actor to Tier to Impact](threat-model-juice-shop-thorough.figure2.svg)

**Threat actors.** The actors below drive the numbered attack paths in the figures above. The **Shop User** is the *victim* of client-side attacks (XSS / CSRF), not an attacker - in Figure 2 the compromise surfaces as the resulting business-impact node rather than as a separate actor box.

- **Shop User** — legitimate customer; target of client-side attacks; target of ⑥ Output Encoding / Cross-Site Scripting, ⑦ CSRF / Permissive CORS.
- **Anonymous Internet Attacker** — no account; registers in seconds when needed; drives ① Insecure Query Construction & Data Access, ② Hardcoded Secrets & Weak Cryptography, ③ Broken Authorization & Access Control, ④ Sensitive File & Secret Exposure, ⑤ Remote Code Execution (unsafe eval).

**7 structural threats**, grouped by weakness class - each row is one threat, not one finding. *Threat Description* states the general architectural weakness (STRIDE in brackets); *Findings* lists the concrete instances, each linked to [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register) with its component; *Risk & Impact* combines severity with business consequence.

| <a id="path-cross-site-scripting"></a>⑥ | **Output Encoding / Cross-Site Scripting** _(T·I)_<br/>attacker-controlled content is rendered in the victim's browser without sanitization; combined with session tokens held in JavaScript-readable storage, any payload yields immediate account takeover. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-015](#f-015)</span> - Cross-Site Scripting (`search-result.component.ts:143`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-01](#c-01)</span>&nbsp;Angular SPA Frontend<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-023](#f-023)</span> - JWT session token stored in localStorage readable (`request.interceptor.ts:16`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-01](#c-01)</span>&nbsp;Angular SPA Frontend | 🟠 **High**<br/>Customer Session Hijack | <span style="white-space:nowrap">◕ [M-020](#m-020)</span><br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">◑ [M-028](#m-028)</span> |
| <a id="path-cross-site-request-forgery"></a>⑦ | **CSRF / Permissive CORS** _(S·T)_<br/>a permissive CORS policy plus missing anti-CSRF tokens let any external page issue authenticated state-changing requests in the victim's session. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🟡&nbsp;[F-050](#f-050)</span> - Wildcard CORS and missing CSP/HSTS response headers (`server.ts:183`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-03](#c-03)</span>&nbsp;Express\.js REST API Backend | 🟡 **Medium**<br/>Customer Session Hijack | <span style="white-space:nowrap">◑ [M-053](#m-053)</span> |

_STRIDE: S spoofing · T tampering · R repudiation · I information disclosure · D denial of service · E elevation of privilege. Risk, findings, components, impact and Fix are derived deterministically; only the one-line weakness description is authored._

**Verified attack chains.** 3 fully viable ([AC-T-003](#ac-t-003), [AC-T-005](#ac-t-005), [AC-T-006](#ac-t-006)); 2 partially blocked ([AC-T-001](#ac-t-001), [AC-T-004](#ac-t-004)). These chains combine individual findings into end-to-end exploitation paths verified step-by-step against the code - see [§9 Abuse Cases](#9-abuse-cases) for the per-step breakdown and blocking mitigations.

### Top Mitigations

Highest-impact P1/P2 mitigations - 15 of 45 qualifying (62 total). Full detail in [§10 Mitigation Register](#10-mitigation-register). All 15 mitigation(s) that fix a Critical finding are always listed here.

| # | Component | Mitigation | Addresses | Effort |
|---|----------------------|------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------|------|
| **1** | [C-01](#c-01) — Angular SPA Frontend | ● [M-008](#m-008) — Harden the authentication flow (`oauth.component.ts:30`) | 🔴 [F-003](#f-003) — OAuth password derived deterministically from email (`oauth.component.ts`) | Medium |
| **2** | [C-02](#c-02) — Authentication and Identity Service | ● [M-011](#m-011) — Use parameterized database queries (`login.ts:34`) | 🔴 [F-006](#f-006) — SQL Injection in login query (`routes/login.ts`) | Low |
| **3** | [C-02](#c-02) — Authentication and Identity Service | ● [M-009](#m-009) — Move cryptographic keys to a managed secret store (`insecurity.ts:21`) | 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) — Hardcoded RSA Signing Key (`lib/insecurity.ts`) | Medium |
| **4** | [C-02](#c-02) — Authentication and Identity Service | ● [M-010](#m-010) — Enforce JWT signature and algorithm verification (`insecurity.ts:55`) | 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — Insecure JWT Verification (`lib/insecurity.ts`) | Medium |
| **5** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ● [M-006](#m-006) — Force role to customer on self-registration and strip client-supplied privileged (`server.ts:408`) | 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields (`server.ts`) | Low |
| **6** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ● [M-013](#m-013) — Use parameterized database queries (`search.ts:23`) | 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — SQL injection (`routes/search.ts`) | Low |
| **7** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ● [M-012](#m-012) — Enforce object-level (ownership) authorization (`address.ts:11`) | 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Insecure Direct Object Reference (`routes/address.ts`) | Medium |
| **8** | [C-01](#c-01) — Angular SPA Frontend | ◕ [M-020](#m-020) — Encode output instead of bypassing the framework sanitizer (`search-result.component.ts:143`) | 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — Cross-Site Scripting (`search-result.component.ts`) | Low |
| **9** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ◕ [M-024](#m-024) — Use parameterized database queries (`showProductReviews.ts:36`) | 🔴 [F-019](#f-019) — NoSQL Injection (`routes/showProductReviews.ts`) | Low |
| **10** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ◕ [M-041](#m-041) — Key the rate limiter on a trusted client identifier, not a client-supplied header (`server.ts:346`) | 🔴 [F-038](#f-038) — Rate Limiter Keyed on Spoofable Forwarded Header (`server.ts`) | Low |
| **11** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ◕ [M-017](#m-017) — Require authentication on every exposed endpoint (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:23`) | 🔴 [F-012](#f-012) — Unauthenticated WebSocket Channel (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts`) | Medium |
| **12** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ◕ [M-045](#m-045) — Enforce server-side authorization on every endpoint (`server.ts:310`) | 🔴 [F-042](#f-042) — Sensitive Routes Registered Without Authentication Middleware (`server.ts`) | Medium |
| **13** | [C-03](#c-03) — Express\.js REST API Backend | ◕ [M-047](#m-047) — Remove server-side evaluation of untrusted input (`b2bOrder.ts:23`) | 🔴 [F-044](#f-044) — Server-side code execution (`routes/b2bOrder.ts`) | Medium |
| **14** | [C-05](#c-05) — Socket\.IO Real-Time Server | ◕ [M-048](#m-048) — Enforce server-side authorization on every endpoint (`chat.ts:176`) | 🔴 [F-045](#f-045) — Excessive LLM Agency in Coupon Generation (`routes/chat.ts`) | Medium |
| **15** | [C-08](#c-08) — Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface | ◕ [M-040](#m-040) — Move secrets to a managed secret store (`checkKeys.ts:10`) | 🔴 [F-037](#f-037) — Hardcoded BIP-39 mnemonic in source (`routes/checkKeys.ts`) | Medium |

*30 additional P1/P2 mitigations capped from the leader-board · 17 P3 backlog items in [§10 Mitigation Register](#10-mitigation-register). Sorted by priority (P1 first), then component, then leverage (most findings first), severity (Critical first), and effort (Low first).*

### Operational Strengths

Operational controls rated Adequate or Partial - grouped into broad clusters (full per-control breakdown in [§7](#7-security-architecture)). Clusters demoted to Weak by open Critical/High findings appear in [§7](#7-security-architecture) instead, not here.

| Strength | What's in Place | Effectiveness | Gap | Mitigates |
|----------------------|----------------------|-------------|--------|----------------|
| **Container & Supply-Chain Hardening** | _Build-time and runtime hardening - minimal base image, non-root execution, dependency inventory._<br/>Automated SCA scanning<br/>Dependency Management and Supply Chain | ✅ Adequate | - | - |


**Bottom line:** These controls narrow specific attack surfaces but none eliminates a Critical finding on its own.

<a id="critical-attack-chain"></a>
<a id="critical-attack-tree"></a>
## Critical Attack Tree

The root is the worst-case attacker goal; below it, each capability branch groups the Critical findings that achieve it. Branches feed the goal by OR - any single path suffices.

```mermaid
graph LR
    G_ROOT["Full admin takeover and database exfiltration"]:::goal
    OR_AUTH["Obtain admin session"]:::or_node
    AND_JWT["Forge admin JWT offline"]:::and_node
    L_T004["F-004 - Hardcoded RSA signing key"]:::leaf
    L_T005["F-005 - JWT algorithm not pinned"]:::leaf
    OR_BYPASS["Bypass credential check"]:::or_node
    L_T006["F-006 - SQL injection in login query"]:::leaf
    L_T003["F-003 - Deterministic OAuth password"]:::leaf
    OR_PRIV["Escalate or exfiltrate"]:::or_node
    L_T001["F-001 - Mass assignment on registration"]:::leaf
    L_T007["F-007 - IDOR across user accounts"]:::leaf
    L_T008["F-008 - SQL injection in search"]:::leaf

    OR_AUTH -->|"OR"| G_ROOT
    OR_PRIV -->|"OR"| G_ROOT
    AND_JWT -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    OR_BYPASS -->|"OR"| OR_AUTH
    L_T004 -->|"AND"| AND_JWT
    L_T005 -->|"AND"| AND_JWT
    L_T006 -->|"OR"| OR_BYPASS
    L_T003 -->|"OR"| OR_BYPASS
    L_T001 -->|"OR"| OR_PRIV
    L_T007 -->|"OR"| OR_PRIV
    L_T008 -->|"OR"| OR_PRIV

    classDef goal fill:#0f172a,stroke:#000,color:#fff,stroke-width:3px
    classDef and_node fill:#334155,stroke:#1e293b,color:#fff,stroke-width:2px
    classDef or_node fill:#64748b,stroke:#334155,color:#fff,stroke-width:2px
    classDef leaf fill:#f3dada,stroke:#b71c1c,color:#7f0000,stroke-width:2px
```

**Findings** (full detail in [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register)): 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) Hardcoded RSA signing key · 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) JWT algorithm not pinned · 🔴 [F-006](#f-006) SQL injection in login query · 🔴 [F-003](#f-003) Deterministic OAuth password · 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) Mass assignment on registration · 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) IDOR across user accounts · 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) SQL injection in search

---

## 1. System Overview

Probably the most modern and sophisticated insecure web application

**Repository:** https://github.com/juice-shop/juice-shop.git
**Runtime:** Node\.js 22 - 26

### Scope

This threat model covers 8 components of juice-shop: **Angular SPA Frontend**, **Authentication and Identity Service**, **Express\.js REST API Backend**, **SQLite3/Sequelize Data Layer**, **Socket\.IO Real-Time Server**, **File System / FTP Storage**, **GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline**, **Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface**.

All 8 modeled components received full STRIDE threat analysis.

**Out of scope:** third-party hosted dependencies, browser runtime, operating-system kernel, and the underlying network infrastructure.

---

<a id="identified-actors"></a>
### Identified Actors

The consolidated threat actors that drive this model - the same set named in the Management Summary. Each row aggregates the findings reachable from that actor's position; the **Shop User** appears as the *victim* of client-side attacks, not an attacker.

| Actor | Role | Reach | Findings | Components |
|----------------------|--------|----------------------|----------------|----------------------|
| Shop User | victim | legitimate customer; target of client-side<br/>attacks | 3 | angular-frontend, express-backend, web3-nft |
| Anonymous Internet Attacker | attacker | no account; registers in seconds when needed | 49 | angular-frontend, auth-service,<br/>ci-cd-pipeline, express-backend,<br/>file-storage, sqlite-data-layer, web3-nft |
| Authenticated Internet Attacker | attacker | owns a regular account; logged in | 9 | angular-frontend, auth-service,<br/>express-backend, socket-io-server,<br/>sqlite-data-layer |

---

## 2. Architecture Diagrams

### 2.1 System Context

Who interacts with juice-shop from the outside, and through which channels. Solid arrows show normal usage; dashed red arrows mark unauthenticated probing or exploit paths (C4 Level 1).

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    USER["End User<br/>(browser)"]
    ATTACKER["Anonymous<br/>Internet Attacker"]
    ADMIN["Admin User"]
    SYSTEM["juice-shop"]
    EXTERNAL["External HTTP Services<br/>(SSRF target)"]
    USER -->|HTTPS · normal usage| SYSTEM
    ATTACKER -.->|HTTPS · probing / exploit| SYSTEM
    ADMIN -->|HTTPS · admin actions| SYSTEM
    SYSTEM -->|outbound · HTTPS| EXTERNAL
    classDef user     fill:#e8f1ea,stroke:#2e7d32,color:#1b5e20,stroke-width:1.5px
    classDef attacker fill:#f3dada,stroke:#b71c1c,color:#7f0000,stroke-width:2px
    classDef admin    fill:#fef3c7,stroke:#b45309,color:#78350f,stroke-width:1.5px
    classDef sys      fill:#f2f2f2,stroke:#424242,color:#111,stroke-width:1.5px
    classDef ext      fill:#f2f2f2,stroke:#9e9e9e,color:#424242,stroke-dasharray:3 3,stroke-width:1px
    class USER user
    class ATTACKER attacker
    class ADMIN admin
    class SYSTEM sys
    class EXTERNAL ext
```

**Key takeaway:** Every actor in the context interacts with juice-shop through its external interface, so authentication and input validation at that edge govern the entire attack surface.

How the system decomposes into deployable units. Each box is a separate runtime process or service container; arrows show synchronous request paths between them. Components with ≥3 Critical findings carry a red border, ≥2 High amber (C4 Level 2).

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    subgraph Client

        sqlite_data_layer[("SQLite3/Sequelize Data Layer")]
    end
    angular_frontend -->|HTTPS REST| auth_service
    auth_service -->|driver| sqlite_data_layer

    auth_service -->|in-process| socket_io_server
    auth_service -->|in-process| file_storage

    auth_service -->|in-process| web3_nft

    class express_backend critical
    class angular_frontend warning
    class sqlite_data_layer warning
    class socket_io_server warning
    class file_storage warning
    class ci_cd_pipeline warning
    class web3_nft warning
```

**Key takeaway:** The system decomposes into 1 client, 6 application and 1 data unit(s); Express\.js REST API Backend carries the most Critical findings (3) and bounds the worst-case blast radius.

### 2.4 Technology Architecture

The technology stack the system is built on. Each box names the framework or runtime that fills that role; per-component findings live in the [§2.3](#23-components) component table above, and the full per-finding catalogue is in [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register).

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    subgraph CLIENT["Client Tier"]

    end
    subgraph APP["Application Tier"]

    end
    subgraph DATA["Data Tier"]
        ORM["fa:fa-database Sequelize ORM<br/><i>object-relational mapper</i>"]:::risk
        SQLITE[("fa:fa-database SQLite<br/><i>embedded relational DB</i>")]:::risk

    end
    subgraph INFRA["Cross-Cutting"]
        INFRA_RUN["fa:fa-cube Docker<br/><i>container runtime</i>"]:::ok
        INFRA_SCM["fa:fa-code-branch GitHub (public)<br/><i>source supply chain</i>"]:::risk

    FE_ANGULAR -->|"HTTPS · JWT"| AUTH_MW
    AUTH_MW -->|"middleware chain"| EXPRESS
    EXPRESS -->|"DB driver"| ORM

    classDef ok fill:#e8f1ea,stroke:#2e7d32,color:#1b5e20,stroke-width:1.5px

    linkStyle 5,6 stroke:#9e9e9e,stroke-width:1px,stroke-dasharray:3 3
```

**Key takeaway:** The stack spans 1 data-tier store(s) behind the application tier; injection and data-at-rest exposure track the data tier, detailed per finding in [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register).

> **Legend:** **red border** ≥ 3 Critical threats on the component · **amber border** ≥ 2 High threats

---

## 3. Attack Walkthroughs

This section walks through how the highest-risk findings are exploited - one short walkthrough per Critical, each with attack steps, a focused sequence diagram, and the primary mitigation. The cross-finding view (which weaknesses combine toward the worst-case goal, and where one fix severs several paths) is in the [Critical Attack Tree](#critical-attack-tree). Full per-finding context - severity rationale, assets, detection signals - is in the [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register) row for each finding.

### 3.1 Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields in Express js REST API Backend

**Source:** 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) — `server.ts:408`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)). STRIDE: Elevation of Privilege. See [§8 F-001](#f-001) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. Self-registration is POST /api/Users, handled by the auto-generated Sequelize/finale REST endpoint.
2. The pre-processing middleware at `server.ts:408-419` only trims email/password/passwordRepeat and never strips extra attributes, so the request body is passed through to model creation intact.
3. The User model (`models/user.ts:79-84`) exposes a writable role attribute whose only guard is isIn ['customer','deluxe','accounting','admin'] - which permits 'admin'.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: express-backend - server.ts:408
    Attacker->>App: The attacker sends a crafted request targeting server.ts line 408
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: The attacker reads the response confirming the weakness - CWE-915
    alt Current state — F-001
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-001
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-006 — Force role to customer on self-registration and strip client
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-006](#m-006) (Force role to customer on self-registration and strip client) lands, 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) is exploitable at `server.ts:408` (Critical-severity, [CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-006](#m-006) (Force role to customer on self-registration and strip client-supplied privileged)

### 3.2 Insecure JWT Verification in Authentication and Identity Service

**Source:** 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — `lib/insecurity.ts:55`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§8 F-005](#f-005) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. Token verification is split across two weak paths. `verify()` at `insecurity.ts:55` calls `jws.verify(token, publicKey)` without passing an allowed-algorithm list, and `isAuthorized()` at `insecurity.ts:52` builds express-jwt@0.1.3 with only { secret: publicKey } and no algorithms option.
2. Neither pins RS256.
3. An attacker crafts a token whose header sets the algorithm to 'none' (empty signature) or to HS256 using the well-known RSA public key (encryptionkeys/jwt.pub) as the HMAC secret.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: auth-service - lib/insecurity.ts:55
    Attacker->>App: The attacker sends a crafted request targeting lib/insecurity.ts line 55
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: The attacker reads the response confirming the weakness - CWE-347
    alt Current state — F-005
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-005
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-010 — Enforce JWT signature and algorithm verification
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-010](#m-010) (Enforce JWT signature and algorithm verification) lands, 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) is exploitable at `lib/insecurity.ts:55` (Critical-severity, [CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-010](#m-010) (Enforce JWT signature and algorithm verification)

### 3.3 SQL Injection in login query in Login

**Source:** 🔴 [F-006](#f-006) — `routes/login.ts:34`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§8 F-006](#f-006) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. An attacker submits the login form with the email field set to ' OR 1=1--.
2. Because `req.body.email` is concatenated directly into the query string at `routes/login.ts:34` (`SELECT * FROM Users WHERE email = '<email>' AND password = '<md5hash>' AND deletedAt IS NULL)`, the injected clause short-circuits the WHERE predicate.
3. The query returns the first Users row - the seeded admin account - and `login.ts:47` issues a valid RS256 JWT for that user.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant API
    participant DB
    Note over API: auth-service - routes/login.ts:34
    Note over DB: Database
    Attacker->>API: Crafted HTTP request to the affected endpoint with classical OR 1=1 payload
    API->>DB: SQL built by string interpolation - payload becomes query
    DB-->>API: First matching row regardless of intended predicate
    API-->>Attacker: 200 OK with authenticated session / leaked rows
    alt Current state — F-006
        Attacker->>API: The attacker sends the exploit for F-006
        API-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-011 — Use parameterized database queries
        Attacker->>API: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        API-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-011](#m-011) (Use parameterized database queries) lands, 🔴 [F-006](#f-006) is exploitable at `routes/login.ts:34` (Critical-severity, [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-011](#m-011) (Use parameterized database queries)

### 3.4 SQL injection in Search

**Source:** 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — `routes/search.ts:23`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§8 F-008](#f-008) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. `searchProducts()` interpolates `req.query.q` directly into a raw `sequelize.query` string: `SELECT * FROM Products WHERE ((name LIKE '%${criteria}%' OR description LIKE '%${criteria}%') …`.
2. The only guard is a 200-char truncation.
3. An unauthenticated caller hits GET /rest/products/search?q=')) UNION SELECT … -- and reads arbitrary tables.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant API
    participant DB
    Note over API: express-backend - routes/search.ts:23
    Note over DB: Database
    Attacker->>API: GET /rest/products/search with classical OR 1=1 payload
    API->>DB: SQL built by string interpolation - payload becomes query
    DB-->>API: First matching row regardless of intended predicate
    API-->>Attacker: 200 OK with authenticated session / leaked rows
    alt Current state — F-008
        Attacker->>API: The attacker sends the exploit for F-008
        API-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-013 — Use parameterized database queries
        Attacker->>API: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        API-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-013](#m-013) (Use parameterized database queries) lands, 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) is exploitable at `routes/search.ts:23` (Critical-severity, [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-013](#m-013) (Use parameterized database queries)

### 3.5 Hardcoded RSA Signing Key in Authentication and Identity Service

**Source:** 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) — `lib/insecurity.ts:21`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§8 F-004](#f-004) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The 1024-bit RSA private key used to sign every session JWT is embedded verbatim at `lib/insecurity.ts:21` and committed to the public OWASP Juice Shop GitHub repository.
2. An attacker clones the repo, copies the PEM block, and signs a JWT offline with { data: { id: 1, email: 'admin@juice-`sh.op`', role: 'admin' }, algorithm: 'RS256' }.
3. Because `authorize()` at `insecurity.ts:54` and the express-jwt middleware at `insecurity.ts:52` both trust this key pair, the forged token is accepted as a fully authenticated admin session - no login, no SQLi, no interaction with the server needed.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant Repo
    participant App
    Note over Repo: Public repository
    Note over App: auth-service - lib/insecurity.ts:21
    Attacker->>Repo: Clone or browse - extract private key from lib/insecurity.ts line 21
    Attacker->>Attacker: Sign forged token / signature with the extracted key
    Attacker->>App: Submit forged artefact in normal authentication flow
    App-->>Attacker: Request accepted as authentic - signature validates
    alt Current state — F-004
        Attacker->>Repo: The attacker sends the exploit for F-004
        Repo-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-009 — Move cryptographic keys to a managed secret store
        Attacker->>Repo: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        Repo-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-009](#m-009) (Move cryptographic keys to a managed secret store) lands, 🔴 [F-004](#f-004) is exploitable at `lib/insecurity.ts:21` (Critical-severity, [CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-009](#m-009) (Move cryptographic keys to a managed secret store)

### 3.6 OAuth password derived deterministically from email in OAuth

**Source:** 🔴 [F-003](#f-003) — `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§8 F-003](#f-003) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. After OAuth login, OAuthComponent computes a local account password as `btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))` (`oauth.component.ts:30`, repeated at line 46) - base64 of the user's email reversed.
2. This value is saved as the account password via `userService.save()` and reused on the normal password login endpoint.
3. The password is therefore a pure, public function of the email address: any attacker who knows a victim's email can compute their exact password offline (`btoa(reverse(email))`) and authenticate through the standard /rest/user/login form without ever touching the OAuth provider.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: angular-frontend - frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30
    Attacker->>App: The attacker sends a crafted request targeting frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts line 30
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: The attacker reads the response confirming the weakness - CWE-287
    alt Current state — F-003
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-003
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-008 — Harden the authentication flow
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-008](#m-008) (Harden the authentication flow) lands, 🔴 [F-003](#f-003) is exploitable at `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30` (Critical-severity, [CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-008](#m-008) (Harden the authentication flow)

### 3.7 Insecure Direct Object Reference in Address

**Source:** 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — `routes/address.ts:11`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-639](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/639.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§8 F-007](#f-007) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The attacker crafts a request targeting the weak spot at `routes/address.ts:11`.
2. Server-side authorization MUST derive the resource owner from the authenticated session (`req.user` / `req.session` / `req.auth`), never from attacker-controlled request data.
3. Trusting `req.body.UserId` etc. enables horizontal privilege escalation across all authenticated tenants.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: express-backend - routes/address.ts:11
    Attacker->>App: The attacker sends a crafted request targeting routes/address.ts line 11
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: The attacker reads the response confirming the weakness - CWE-639
    alt Current state — F-007
        Attacker->>App: The attacker sends the exploit for F-007
        App-->>Attacker: Exploit succeeds
    else After M-012 — Enforce object-level (ownership) authorization
        Attacker->>App: The attacker retries the same request after the fix
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until ● [M-012](#m-012) (Enforce object-level (ownership) authorization) lands, 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) is exploitable at `routes/address.ts:11` (Critical-severity, [CWE-639](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/639.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: ● [M-012](#m-012) (Enforce object-level (ownership) authorization)

## 5. Attack Surface

Network-reachable entry points classified by authentication requirement. Each row links to the threat(s) referenced in its **Notes** column. The **Risk** column reflects the highest-severity linked finding. Entry points with no linked finding are still listed when they sit on a sensitive surface (authentication, registration, management) or look like a missing-auth/authz suspect - marked **⚑ Review** in Notes.

### 5.1 Unauthenticated Entry Points (60)

| Method | Route | Risk | Notes |
|------|----------------------------------------|----------|------------------------------------|
| POST | `/rest/user/login` | 🔴 Critical | 🔴 [F-003](#f-003) — OAuth password derived deterministically from email (`oauth.component.ts:30`)<br/>🟠 [F-010](#f-010) — Missing Brute-Force Protection on Login (`server.ts:596`)<br/>🔴 [F-006](#f-006) — SQL Injection in login query (`login.ts:34`)<br/>Primary authentication endpoint. Accepts email+password, issues JWT. Vulnerable to SQL injection and brute force (no rate limiting by default). Unauthenticated. |
| POST | `/api/Users (Registration)` | 🔴 Critical | 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields (`server.ts:408`)<br/>User self-registration endpoint. Accepts email, password, and optional admin role (mass assignment vulnerability). No email verification. Unauthenticated. |
| GET | `/rest/products/search` | 🔴 Critical | 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — SQL injection (`search.ts:23`)<br/>🟡 [F-058](#f-058) — Missing rate limiting and parser-bomb guards on public endpoints (`server.ts:343`)<br/>handler: `server.ts:602` |
| POST | `/file-upload` | 🟠 High | 🟠 [F-021](#f-021) — Path Traversal (`fileUpload.ts:33`)<br/>🟠 [F-018](#f-018) — XXE external-entity processing on XML upload (`xml.ts:37`)<br/>🟡 [F-058](#f-058) — Missing rate limiting and parser-bomb guards on public endpoints (`server.ts:343`)<br/>Unrestricted file upload to /uploads/ directory. Accepts any file type despite MIME check (bypass via crafted headers). Authenticated but file type not strictly enforced. Path traversal in filename possible. |
| POST | `/profile` | 🟠 High | 🟠 [F-031](#f-031) — SSRF (`profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`)<br/>handler: `server.ts:667` |
| POST | `/profile/image/file` | 🟠 High | 🟠 [F-031](#f-031) — SSRF (`profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`)<br/>🟡 [F-051](#f-051) — Content-Type-only upload filter on /rest/memories (`server.ts:701`)<br/>handler: `server.ts:310` |

## 7. Security Architecture

This chapter is organized by security-control category. The architecture section avoids artificial control IDs and finding-ID columns in overview tables. Findings are listed only where the affected control is described.

_[§7](#7-security-architecture) schema v2 (13-section control-category layout). Cataloged controls: 24 total - 1 adequate, 3 partial, 7 weak, 8 unsafe, 5 missing. Linked threats: 61._

**How to read the verdicts.** Every control category (and every sub-control below it) carries exactly one status. The two red verdicts do **not** mean the same thing - this is the distinction that decides what you have to do about a finding:

| Status | Meaning | What it asks of you |
|----------|------------------------------------|------------------------|
| 🟢 Adequate | Control is present and sound | Nothing - keep it |
| 🟡 Partial | Present, but with meaningful gaps | Close the gap |
| 🟠 Weak | Present, but has exploitable gaps | Strengthen it |
| 🔴 Unsafe | **Present and relied upon, but defeated /<br/>trivially bypassable** | **Fix the existing control** |
| 🔴 Missing | **Control was never built** | **Add the control** |
| - | Not applicable to this codebase | - |

So "🔴 Unsafe" on a control category does *not* mean the control is absent - it means the control exists but does not hold (`e.g`. an MD5 password hash, a raw-SQL query path, a hardcoded signing key). "🔴 Missing" is reserved for controls that were never built (`e.g`. no Content-Security-Policy header).
