#### F-013 · TOTP 2FA secret stored in plaintext (models/user.ts:112)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - SQLite3/Sequelize Data Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/user.ts:112`

**Issue:** The User model declares `totpSecret` as a plain `DataTypes.STRING` (default '') with no encryption hook, and `datacreator.ts:200` seeds it directly. The shared TOTP seed is the single factor that makes 2FA meaningful; storing it in cleartext means any actor who reads the Users table - insider ACT-D-04 with local-fs, or an attacker who exfiltrates the unencrypted DB file - can regenerate valid time-based codes for every 2FA-enrolled account and silently defeat multi-factor authentication.

This is the twoFactorAuthUnsafeSecretStorage weakness. Attackers with DB read can mint valid 2FA codes, nullifying multi-factor authentication.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - totpSecret is defined as an unencrypted STRING column with defaultValue '' and no `set()` encryption hook.

```typescript
// models/user.ts:112
        defaultValue: '/assets/public/images/uploads/default.svg'
      },
      totpSecret: {
        type: DataTypes.STRING,
        defaultValue: ''
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-018](#m-018) — Stop storing sensitive data in cleartext (`user.ts:112`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-312](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/312.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-037"></a><a id="f-037"></a>
#### F-037 · Hardcoded BIP-39 mnemonic in source (routes/checkKeys.ts:10)

**Severity:** 🟠 High - secret committed to the public source repo - extractable on clone, no prior access needed  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/checkKeys.ts:10`

**Issue:** `checkKeys.ts:10` embeds a literal 12-word BIP-39 mnemonic ('purpose betray marriage blame crunch monitor spin slide donate sport lift clutch') that is loaded at request time and deterministically derived into a private key, public key and address via `HDNodeWallet.fromPhrase()`. Because the phrase ships in the public repository, any actor who reads the source recovers the full HD wallet seed and every private key derivable from it.

The /rest/web3/submitKey handler even confirms a correct guess by returning success, so the secret is both disclosed in source and oracle-verifiable at runtime. Full compromise of the derived Ethereum wallet's private key; any funds or NFT ownership tied to that seed are controllable by anyone who reads the repo.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The mnemonic constant at `checkKeys.ts:10` is passed to `HDNodeWallet.fromPhrase()` at line 11, deriving privateKey at line 12 - the seed material lives in committed source, not in an env var or vault.

```typescript
// routes/checkKeys.ts:10
    try {
      const { HDNodeWallet } = await import('ethers')
      const mnemonic = 'purpose betray marriage blame crunch monitor spin slide donate sport lift clutch'
      const mnemonicWallet = HDNodeWallet.fromPhrase(mnemonic)
      const privateKey = mnemonicWallet.privateKey
```

**Fix:** Move the credential out of source control into a secret store and rotate it → ◕ [M-040](#m-040) — Move secrets to a managed secret store (`checkKeys.ts:10`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-002"></a><a id="f-002"></a>
#### F-002 · Client-side-only route guards decide admin access in the (app.guard.ts:52)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/app.guard.ts:52`

**Issue:** AdminGuard and AccountingGuard make authorization decisions entirely in the browser: `LoginGuard.tokenDecode()` calls `jwtDecode(token)` (`app.guard.ts:38`) - which decodes but does NOT verify the JWT signature - and the guards then check `payload.data.role === roles.admin` (`app.guard.ts:54`) / `roles.accounting` (:70). Two weaknesses stem from this.

(1) The gate is client-enforced: an attacker who calls the underlying REST endpoints directly bypasses the guard entirely, so the guard provides only UX, not security - safe only if every backend route independently enforces authorization. Low-privilege or anonymous users reach privileged UI and any endpoint lacking independent server-side authorization is exploitable.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - AdminGuard reads a role claim from an unverified `jwtDecode()` result and grants the admin route on a pure client-side comparison.

**Fix:** ◕ [M-007](#m-007) — Treat route guards as UX-only and enforce role authorization on every server endpoint (`app.guard.ts:52`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-602](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/602.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

#### F-009 · OAuth implicit flow leaks access_token

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:71`

**Issue:** `OAuthComponent.parseRedirectUrlParams()` reads the OAuth response from the URL hash fragment (`route.snapshot.data.params`) and splits out an `access_token` (`oauth.component.ts:71-78`) - the implicit grant (response_type=token). There is no `state` parameter checked, no `nonce`, and no PKCE code_verifier.

Two consequences follow. Attacker can bind a victim's session to an attacker identity (login CSRF) or capture the access token from the URL context.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `parseRedirectUrlParams()` manually parses the hash for `access_token` with no `state`/`nonce`/PKCE validation before calling `oauthLogin()`.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:71

  parseRedirectUrlParams () {
    const hash = this.route.snapshot.data.params.substr(1)
    const splitted = hash.split('&')
    const params: any = {}
```

**Fix:** ◑ [M-014](#m-014) — Replace OAuth implicit grant with Authorization Code + PKCE and validate a CSRF state (`oauth.component.ts:71`)

**Classification:** OAuth / OIDC Misconfiguration · [CWE-598](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/598.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-010"></a><a id="f-010"></a>
#### F-010 · Missing Brute-Force Protection on Login (server.ts:596)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:596`

**Issue:** The login route is registered as `app.post('/rest/user/login', login())` with no rate-limiting or account-lockout middleware - contrast the reset-password route and the 2FA routes at `server.ts:458-473`, which do carry `rateLimit()`. An attacker runs an automated credential-stuffing or password-spraying campaign against /rest/user/login at full speed.

Because passwords are stored as unsalted MD5 (see 🟠 [F-026](#f-026)) and there is no lockout, offline-derived candidate passwords can be validated online rapidly, and there is no throttle to slow guessing of weak seeded accounts (admi**** (8 chars), etc.). Unlimited online password guessing enabling account takeover of weak-credential accounts.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - No `rateLimit()`/lockout middleware wraps `app.post`('/rest/user/login') at `server.ts:596`, unlike the reset-password and 2FA endpoints.

```typescript
// server.ts:596

  /* Custom Restful API */
  app.post('/rest/user/login', login())
  app.get('/rest/user/change-password', utils.asyncHandler(changePassword()))
  app.post('/rest/user/reset-password', utils.asyncHandler(resetPassword()))
```

**Fix:** Apply rate limiting and lock-out thresholds on authentication endpoints → ◕ [M-015](#m-015) — Rate-limit and lock out repeated authentication attempts (`server.ts:596`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-307](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/307.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

**Issue:** `resetPassword.ts` lets any unauthenticated caller set a new password for an account by supplying only the target email plus the answer to that account's security question (checked via `security.hmac`(answer) === `data.answer`). ```typescript

```typescript
        }]
      })
      if ((data != null) && security.hmac(answer) === data.answer) {
        const user = await UserModel.findByPk(data.UserId)
        if (user) {
```

<a id="t-016"></a><a id="f-016"></a>
#### F-016 · Npm lifecycle scripts execute on CI/Docker install

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `Dockerfile:5`

**Issue:** `package.json:56` defines a `postinstall` hook (`cd frontend && npm install && ... npm run build:frontend ...`), and most install steps run plain `npm install` without `--ignore-scripts`: `ci.yml` lines 51, 71, 110, 146, 203, 238, 292, and `Dockerfile:5` (`npm install --omit=dev`).

Combined with the missing lockfile (🟠 [F-017](#f-017)), any direct or transitive dependency's own `preinstall`/`install`/`postinstall` script executes arbitrary code - in CI runners that hold job secrets (`ALCHEMY_API_KEY`, `CYPRESS_RECORD_KEY`, `E2E_SOLUTIONS_WEBHOOK`, `GITHUB_TOKEN`) and, in the Dockerfile stage, with the result baked into the published image. A malicious dependency's install hook runs arbitrary code in CI (exposing job secrets) and inside the Docker build layer shipped to users.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `Dockerfile:5` and seven `ci.yml` jobs run `npm install` without `--ignore-scripts`, allowing dependency lifecycle hooks to execute.

```dockerfile
// Dockerfile:5
WORKDIR /juice-shop
RUN npm install -g typescript@^6.0.3
RUN npm install --omit=dev
RUN npm dedupe --omit=dev
RUN rm -rf frontend/node_modules
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-021](#m-021) — Pin third-party dependencies to immutable versions (`Dockerfile:5`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-017"></a><a id="f-017"></a>
#### F-017 · CI/CD Workflow Supply-Chain Risk

**Severity:** 🟠 High _(raw Critical)_  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.npmrc:1`

**Instances (7):** `.npmrc:1`, `.github/workflows/image_actions.yml:33`, `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:23`, `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:34`, `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:36`, `.github/workflows/image_actions.yml:42`, `.github/workflows/ci.yml:188`

**Issue:** `.npmrc:1` sets `package-lock=false`, and no `package-lock.json`/`npm-shrinkwrap.json` exists in the repo. Every CI job in `ci.yml` (coding-challenge-rsn, frontend/server/api-test, custom-config-test, e2e-test, smoke-test) and the Dockerfile installer stage run `npm install` (not `npm ci`), so npm re-resolves every semver range against the live public registry at build time.

An attacker who publishes a malicious in-range version of any direct or transitive dependency (or wins a dependency-confusion race on an internal-looking name) gets their code pulled into the build without any integrity pin. A malicious in-range dependency version executes in CI and is baked into the published Docker image and release artifacts consumed downstream.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `.npmrc:1` disables lockfile generation and no lockfile is committed, so `npm install` in CI resolves version ranges non-deterministically.

```
// .npmrc:1
package-lock=false
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-022](#m-022) — Commit `package-lock.json` and switch CI/Docker installs to npm ci (`.npmrc:1`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-1357](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1357.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-018"></a><a id="f-018"></a>
#### F-018 · XXE external-entity processing on XML upload (lib/xml.ts:37)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `lib/xml.ts:37`

**Issue:** `handleXmlUpload()` forwards uploaded .xml buffers to `parseXmlString()`, which parses with `XML_PARSE_NOENT | XML_PARSE_DTDLOAD` and registers a filesystem input provider (`lib/xml.ts:33-38`). An authenticated B2B user uploads a document declaring `<!ENTITY xxe SYSTEM 'file:///etc/passwd'>` to POST /file-upload; the resolved entity is reflected back verbatim in the deprecation error body (`fileUpload.ts:79`), disclosing arbitrary host files.

A nested-entity (billion-laughs) payload instead trips the 2s vm timeout, yielding a 503. Arbitrary local file disclosure (/etc/passwd, config, keys) and denial of service via entity expansion.

**Root cause:** User input flows into a server-side interpreter (SQL, NoSQL, XML, YAML, LDAP, OS shell) without parameterization or schema validation.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - parseXmlString enables entity substitution + DTD load + host FS access at `lib/xml.ts:37`, and the parsed content is echoed in the response at `fileUpload.ts`:79.

```typescript
// lib/xml.ts:37
  const option = libxml2.ParseOption.XML_PARSE_NOENT | libxml2.ParseOption.XML_PARSE_DTDLOAD | libxml2.ParseOption.XML_PARSE_NOBLANKS | libxml2.ParseOption.XML_PARSE_NOCDATA
  const sandbox = { libxml2, data, option }
  vm.createContext(sandbox)
  const xmlDoc = vm.runInContext('libxml2.XmlDocument.fromString(data, { option })', sandbox, { timeout: timeoutMs })
  const xmlString = xmlDoc.toString()
```

**Fix:** Disable external entity resolution on every XML parser and reject DOCTYPE declarations → ◕ [M-023](#m-023) — Disable XML external entity (XXE) resolution (`xml.ts:37`)

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-021"></a><a id="f-021"></a>
#### F-021 · Path Traversal (routes/fileUpload.ts:33)

**Severity:** 🟠 High _(raw Critical)_  ·  **Component:** [C-06](#c-06) - File System / FTP Storage  ·  **Location:** `routes/fileUpload.ts:33`

**Instances (2):** `routes/fileUpload.ts:33`, `routes/fileServer.ts:29`

**Issue:** A user POSTs a crafted .zip to /file-upload. `extractZipBuffer()` takes each archive entry's `entry.path` verbatim and streams it to `fs.createWriteStream('uploads/complaints/' + fileName)`.

An entry named `../../ftp/legal.md` (or `../../routes/login.ts`) escapes the intended uploads/complaints/ directory. Attacker overwrites arbitrary in-repo files (route handlers, ftp/ documents), enabling code tampering and potential RCE.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The containment check at line 33 tests `absolutePath.includes(path.resolve('.'))` (project root) instead of `path.resolve('uploads/complaints/')`, so `../` sequences in `entry.path` are honored by the write at line 34.

```typescript
// routes/fileUpload.ts:33
    const absolutePath = path.resolve('uploads/complaints/' + fileName)
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.fileWriteChallenge, () => { return absolutePath === path.resolve('ftp/legal.md') })
    if (absolutePath.includes(path.resolve('.'))) {
      await pipeline(entry.stream(), fs.createWriteStream('uploads/complaints/' + fileName))
    }
```

**Fix:** Resolve and normalise every constructed path and reject anything that escapes the intended base directory → ◕ [M-026](#m-026) — Constrain file paths to a safe base directory (`fileUpload.ts:33`)

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-22](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/22.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-022"></a><a id="f-022"></a>

A grep across these files for any logger/audit call returns zero hits.

After an account takeover an attacker can change a victim's password, disable their 2FA, and operate the account with no server-side trail; an incident responder has no way to attribute or reconstruct the sequence, and the victim can plausibly deny (or cannot prove) unauthorized activity. Authentication and credential-change actions are non-attributable and non-reconstructable, defeating incident response and compliance monitoring.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - No audit/log emission exists in `login.ts`, `changePassword.ts`, `resetPassword.ts`, or 2fa.ts (0 matches for logger/audit patterns).

```typescript
// routes/login.ts:18

// vuln-code-snippet start loginAdminChallenge loginBenderChallenge loginJimChallenge
export function login () {
  function afterLogin (user: User, res: Response, next: NextFunction) {
    verifyPostLoginChallenges(user) // vuln-code-snippet hide-line
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-027](#m-027) — Add security audit logging (`login.ts:18`)

**Classification:** Missing Audit Logging & Accountability · [CWE-778](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/778.html) · [OWASP A09:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A09_2021/)

<a id="t-026"></a><a id="f-026"></a>
#### F-026 · Unsalted MD5 Password Hashing (lib/insecurity.ts:41)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Authentication and Identity Service  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:41`

**Issue:** Passwords are hashed with unsalted MD5: `hash()` is crypto.createHash('md5').update(data).digest('hex'), and the User model password setter (`models/user.ts:76`) applies it on every write. MD5 is fast and collision-broken, and the absence of a per-user salt means identical passwords produce identical digests and enable precomputed rainbow-table lookups.

If an attacker obtains the Users table (`e.g`. via the login SQLi in 🔴 [F-006](#f-006)), essentially every password is recoverable in minutes on commodity hardware.

Mass offline recovery of all user passwords once the Users table is exposed; credential reuse amplifies blast radius across other systems.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `lib/insecurity.ts:41` defines the password hash as unsalted MD5; `models/user.ts:76` applies it to every stored password.

**Fix:** Replace the broken hash with a salted password-hashing function (bcrypt/Argon2id) → ◕ [M-031](#m-031) — Hash passwords with a strong, salted algorithm (`insecurity.ts:41`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-916](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/916.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-027"></a><a id="f-027"></a>
#### F-027 · GitHub Actions workflow-level permissions block (update-news-www.yml:1)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/update-news-www.yml:1`

**Instances (14):** `.github/workflows/update-news-www.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/rebase.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/update-challenges-ebook.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/update-news-www-legacy.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/release.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/zap_scan.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/image_actions.yml:1` … (+6 more)

**Issue:** GitHub Actions workflow-level permissions block - .github/workflows/update-news-www.yml:1. Without an explicit permissions block, the workflow inherits the repository default (commonly write-all) for `GITHUB_TOKEN` - any compromised step can push code, create releases, or approve PRs.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.


<a id="t-028"></a><a id="f-028"></a>
#### F-028 · Base image must be digest-pinned

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `Dockerfile:1`

**Issue:** Dockerfile base image must be digest-pinned - Dockerfile:1. Tag-only base images (FROM node:24) can be silently substituted by a malicious publisher. Digest-pinning (@sha256:…) ensures the exact image bytes are used on every build.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified

```dockerfile
// Dockerfile:1
FROM node:24 AS installer
COPY . /juice-shop
WORKDIR /juice-shop
```

**Fix:** Replace the unmaintained dependency with a maintained equivalent or fork it under ownership → ◕ [M-003](#m-003) — Pin the container base image to an immutable digest (`Dockerfile:1`)

<a id="t-029"></a><a id="f-029"></a>
#### F-029 · Path Traversal (routes/fileServer.ts:28)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/fileServer.ts:28`

**Instances (2):** `routes/fileServer.ts:28`, `routes/fileUpload.ts:34`

**Issue:** `servePublicFiles()` allows only .md/.pdf names, then calls `security.cutOffPoisonNullByte(file)` before `res.sendFile(path.resolve('ftp/', file))`. An unauthenticated caller requests GET /ftp/package.json.bak%2500.md: the extension check passes on the .md suffix, the null-byte cutoff strips everything from %00 onward, and sendFile serves ftp/package.json.bak.

The bundled solveIf hooks (lines 42-48) enumerate the sensitive backup/key files this exposes. Unauthenticated disclosure of backup files, key material and other restricted artefacts in the ftp/ directory.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The null-byte truncation at `fileServer.ts:28` defeats the extension allowlist immediately above it, so `non-.md`/.pdf files under ftp/ are served.

```typescript
// routes/fileServer.ts:28
  function verify (file: string, res: Response, next: NextFunction) {
    if (file && (endsWithAllowlistedFileType(file) || (file === 'incident-support.kdbx'))) {
      file = security.cutOffPoisonNullByte(file)

      challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.directoryListingChallenge, () => { return file.toLowerCase() === 'acquisitions.md' })
```

**Fix:** Resolve and normalise every constructed path and reject anything that escapes the intended base directory → ◕ [M-032](#m-032) — Constrain file paths to a safe base directory (`fileServer.ts:28`)

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-22](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/22.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-030"></a><a id="f-030"></a>
#### F-030 · Unauthenticated encryption-key directory exposure (server.ts:277)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:277`

**Issue:** `server.ts:277-278` mounts /encryptionkeys with serveIndex directory browsing plus `serveKeyFiles()`, both without any authorization middleware. `keyServer.ts` only blocks forward slashes before `res.sendFile(path.resolve('encryptionkeys/', file))`.

Any anonymous visitor browses the directory listing and downloads key material (including `jwt.pub`, which pairs with the hardcoded private key finding to complete a token-forgery chain). Public disclosure of cryptographic key files, directly enabling the JWT-forgery chain.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The /encryptionkeys mount at `server.ts:277-278` has no `isAuthorized()` guard and exposes a browsable directory of key files.

**Fix:** Restrict the response to the minimum fields needed and never echo secrets → ◕ [M-033](#m-033) — Stop exposing internal information to clients (`server.ts:277`)

**Classification:** Error Information Disclosure · [CWE-200](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/200.html) · [OWASP A05:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A05_2021/)

#### F-031 · SSRF (routes/profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`

**Issue:** `profileImageUrlUpload()` calls `await fetch(url)` on `req.body.imageUrl` with no scheme or host validation. An authenticated user POSTs /profile/image/url with imageUrl=http://169.254.169.254/latest/meta-data/ or http://localhost:3000/rest/admin/...

and the server issues the request from inside the trust zone. Access to internal-only services and cloud metadata endpoints from the server's network position.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `req.body.imageUrl` is passed directly to `fetch()` at `profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24` with no allowlist.

```typescript
// routes/profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24
      if (loggedInUser) {
        try {
          const response = await fetch(url)
          if (!response.ok || !response.body) {
            throw new Error('url returned a non-OK status code or an empty body')
```

**Fix:** Validate the URL scheme + host against an explicit allow-list before issuing outbound requests → ◕ [M-034](#m-034) — Validate and allowlist outbound request targets (`profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`)

Anonymous disclosure of cryptographic key material, enabling forgery/decryption of protected data.

```typescript
    if (!file.includes('/')) {

      res.status(403)
```

<a id="t-033"></a><a id="f-033"></a>
#### F-033 · FTP directory listing exposes sensitive files (server.ts:269)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:269`

**Issue:** `server.ts:269` registers serveIndex('ftp', { icons: true }) with no authentication, so GET /ftp/ renders a full browsable listing of the ftp/ directory. The listing reveals sensitive artifacts by name - `acquisitions.md` (unannounced M&A letter), `coupons_2013.md.bak`, `package.json.bak` / package-lock.json.bak (dependency/source leakage), `suspicious_errors.yml`, `encrypt.pyc`, and incident-`support.kdbx` (a KeePass credential database).

The `robots.txt` Disallow:/ftp entry (`server.ts:226`) is advisory only and does not restrict access. Attackers enumerate and locate confidential backups, source archives, and a credential vault file.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - serveIndex('ftp') at `server.ts:269` has no auth guard, exposing the directory index of ftp/ which contains backups and a KeePass DB per the on-disk listing.

```typescript
// server.ts:269
  // vuln-code-snippet start directoryListingChallenge accessLogDisclosureChallenge
  /* /ftp directory browsing and file download */ // vuln-code-snippet neutral-line directoryListingChallenge
  app.use('/ftp', serveIndexMiddleware, serveIndex('ftp', { icons: true })) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line directoryListingChallenge
  app.use('/ftp(?!/quarantine)/:file', servePublicFiles()) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line directoryListingChallenge
  app.use('/ftp/quarantine/:file', serveQuarantineFiles()) // vuln-code-snippet neutral-line directoryListingChallenge
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-036](#m-036) — Remove serveIndex directory browsing for /ftp and store non-public files outside the (`server.ts:269`)

**Classification:** Unauthenticated Management Plane · [CWE-548](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/548.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-034"></a><a id="f-034"></a>
#### F-034 · XXE external entity file disclosure (routes/fileUpload.ts:76)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-06](#c-06) - File System / FTP Storage  ·  **Location:** `routes/fileUpload.ts:76`

**Issue:** `handleXmlUpload()` passes the raw buffer of any uploaded .xml file straight into parseXmlString(data) with no entity restriction. An attacker uploads XML with an external entity (`<!ENTITY xxe SYSTEM 'file:///etc/passwd'>`) referenced in the document body.

The parsed string - including the resolved file contents - is echoed back inside the error response at line 79 (`utils.trunc(xmlString, 400)`), giving a direct exfiltration channel for local files such as /etc/passwd or application secrets. Disclosure of arbitrary local files (credentials, /etc/passwd) and denial of service via entity expansion.

**Root cause:** User input flows into a server-side interpreter (SQL, NoSQL, XML, YAML, LDAP, OS shell) without parameterization or schema validation.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - Line 76 calls `parseXmlString(data)` on attacker-supplied XML and line 79 reflects the parsed `xmlString` back to the client, so resolved external-entity content leaves the server in the response body.

```typescript
// routes/fileUpload.ts:76
      const data = file.buffer.toString()
      try {
        const xmlString = await parseXmlString(data)
        challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.xxeFileDisclosureChallenge, () => { return (utils.matchesEtcPasswdFile(xmlString) || utils.matchesSystemIniFile(xmlString)) })
        res.status(410)
```

**Fix:** Disable external entity resolution on every XML parser and reject DOCTYPE declarations → ◕ [M-037](#m-037) — Disable XML external entity (XXE) resolution (`fileUpload.ts:76`)

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-036"></a><a id="f-036"></a>
#### F-036 · SQLite store persisted unencrypted (models/index.ts:41)

**Severity:** 🟠 High _(raw Critical)_  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - SQLite3/Sequelize Data Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/index.ts:41`

**Issue:** The Sequelize connection is opened against a plain on-disk SQLite file (`storage: 'data/juiceshop.sqlite'`) with no SQLCipher key, no `PRAGMA key`, and no filesystem-level encryption. The single file holds every sensitive column in the system: user emails, MD5 password hashes, TOTP 2FA secrets, full payment card numbers, delivery addresses and HMAC'd security answers.

A malicious insider developer (ACT-D-04) with local-fs or CI/CD-runtime access, or any process that can read the working directory, copies `data/juiceshop.sqlite` and exfiltrates the entire customer dataset offline with a stock `sqlite3` client - no application credentials required. Full offline disclosure of all PII, credential material and payment data from a single copied file.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `createSequelize()` sets storage to the plaintext file 'data/juiceshop.sqlite' with no encryption dialectOption; a grep for encrypt/cipher/sqlcipher/pragma-key across models/ returns zero hits.

```typescript
// models/index.ts:41
    },
    transactionType: Transaction.TYPES.IMMEDIATE,
    storage: options?.inMemory ? ':memory:' : 'data/juiceshop.sqlite',
    logging: false
  })
```

**Fix:** Encrypt the data in transit and at rest with vetted primitives → ◕ [M-039](#m-039) — Encrypt the SQLite datastore at rest with SQLCipher and restrict file permissions (`index.ts:41`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-311](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/311.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-038"></a><a id="f-038"></a>
#### F-038 · Rate Limiter Keyed on Spoofable Forwarded Header (server.ts:346)

**Severity:** 🟠 High - elevated as an attack-chain keystone (individual baseline: High)  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:346`

**Issue:** The only brute-force control on password reset uses a rate-limit keyGenerator that trusts the client-supplied X-Forwarded-For header: keyGenerator returns headers['X-Forwarded-For'] ?? ip, and app.enable('trust proxy') makes Express honor it.

An attacker rotates a fresh X-Forwarded-For value on every request, so each request lands in its own rate-limit bucket and the windowMs/max ceiling never trips. Complete bypass of the reset-password rate limit, enabling unthrottled security-answer brute force and reset-endpoint flooding.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `server.ts:346` keys the reset-password limiter on the attacker-controlled X-Forwarded-For header (with trust proxy enabled at :342), so per-attacker limits are trivially evaded.

```typescript
// server.ts:346
    windowMs: 5 * 60 * 1000,
    max: 100,
    keyGenerator ({ headers, ip }: { headers: any, ip: any }) { return headers['X-Forwarded-For'] ?? ip } // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line resetPasswordMortyChallenge
  }))
  // vuln-code-snippet end resetPasswordMortyChallenge
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-041](#m-041) — Key the rate limiter on a trusted client identifier, not a client-supplied header (`server.ts:346`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-290](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/290.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-040"></a><a id="f-040"></a>

There is no rate limiting on /rest/web3/* (rateLimit is applied only to reset-password and 2FA routes in `server.ts`).

An anonymous attacker sends a high-volume stream of requests each with a unique fabricated walletAddress, growing the Set without limit until the Node process exhausts heap memory. Memory-exhaustion crash of the app process and/or depletion of the paid Alchemy API quota, degrading availability for all users.

```typescript

    const metamaskAddress = req.body.walletAddress
    walletsConnected.add(metamaskAddress)
    try {
      if (!isEventListenerCreated) {
```

**Fix:** Bound the request rate and the per-request resource budget on this endpoint → ◕ [M-043](#m-043) — Rate-limit and lock out repeated authentication attempts (`web3Wallet.ts:16`)

<a id="t-041"></a><a id="f-041"></a>
#### F-041 · Password Change Without Current Password (routes/changePassword.ts:39)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Authentication and Identity Service  ·  **Location:** `routes/changePassword.ts:39`

**Issue:** `changePassword.ts` sets the new password after only a conditional current-password check: at line 39 the guard is if `(currentPassword && security.hash(currentPassword) !== loggedInUser.data.password).` When the attacker simply omits the current query parameter, currentPassword is falsy, the entire branch is skipped, and the update proceeds at line 51 with no proof of knowing the existing password. Combined with the endpoint being an idempotent GET (`server.ts:597`, /rest/user/change-password) whose token is read from the Authorization header, an attacker who has hijacked a session (via any of the token-forgery findings above) or who leverages a leaked token can overwrite the victim's password unconditionally and lock them out - the changePasswordBenderChallenge (line 54) exercises exactly this no-current-password path.

Session-holding attacker changes a victim's password without knowing it, achieving persistent account takeover and lockout.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `changePassword.ts:39` makes the current-password check conditional on currentPassword being truthy, so omitting it bypasses verification entirely before the update at line 51.

```typescript
// routes/changePassword.ts:39
    }

    if (currentPassword && security.hash(currentPassword) !== loggedInUser.data.password) {
      res.status(401).send(res.__('Current password is not correct.'))
      return
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-044](#m-044) — Require and verify the current password unconditionally on password change (`changePassword.ts:39`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-620](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/620.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-042"></a><a id="f-042"></a>
#### F-042 · Sensitive Routes Registered Without Authentication Middleware (server.ts:310)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:310`

**Instances (16):** `server.ts:310`, `server.ts:311`, `server.ts:420`, `server.ts:421`, `server.ts:422`, `server.ts:438`, `server.ts:441`, `server.ts:596` … (+8 more)

**Issue:** State-changing operations on sensitive resources MUST require a proven session. A registration line that lacks any auth marker either trusts the URL itself or relies on a downstream check that the static signature cannot prove exists.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - Route-level authorization middleware is missing on a mutating endpoint.

```typescript
// server.ts:310
  /* File Upload */
  app.post('/file-upload', uploadToMemory.single('file'), ensureFileIsPassed, metrics.observeFileUploadMetricsMiddleware(), checkUploadSize, checkFileType, handleZipFileUpload, handleXmlUpload, handleYamlUpload)
  app.post('/profile/image/file', uploadToMemory.single('file'), ensureFileIsPassed, metrics.observeFileUploadMetricsMiddleware(), utils.asyncHandler(profileImageFileUpload()))
  app.post('/profile/image/url', uploadToMemory.single('file'), utils.asyncHandler(profileImageUrlUpload()))
  app.post('/rest/memories', uploadToDisk.single('image'), ensureFileIsPassed, security.appendUserId(), metrics.observeFileUploadMetricsMiddleware(), utils.asyncHandler(addMemory()))
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-045](#m-045) — Enforce server-side authorization on every endpoint (`server.ts:310`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-862](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/862.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-043"></a><a id="f-043"></a>
#### F-043 · No permissions block

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:24`

**Issue:** `ci.yml`, `release.yml`, and `image_actions.yml` declare no top-level or job-level `permissions:` block (grep confirms only `lock.yml`, `codeql-analysis.yml`, and `pr-compliance.yml` scope the token). Absent an explicit block, the automatically-provisioned `GITHUB_TOKEN` inherits the repository/organisation default, which for many repos is read-write on `contents`, `packages`, and more.

If any workflow step is compromised - `e.g`. via the mutable action ref (🟠 [F-017](#f-017)) or a malicious install hook (🟠 [F-016](#f-016)) - the attacker inherits a broad write token and can push commits/tags, create releases, or publish packages, converting build-time code execution into persistent repository and artifact tampering.

A single compromised step wields a repo-write token to push code, tags, or releases, escalating build-time execution to persistent supply-chain tampering.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - None of `ci.yml/release.yml/image_actions.yml` declare a `permissions:` block, so `GITHUB_TOKEN` defaults to the repo-wide (often write) scope.

```yaml
// .github/workflows/ci.yml:24
  NODE_OPTIONS: "--max_old_space_size=4096"
  CYCLONEDX_NPM_VERSION: '^2.0.0||^3.0.0||^4.0.0'   # keep in sync with package.json
jobs:
  lint:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-046](#m-046) — Drop unnecessary privileges in build and runtime (`ci.yml:24`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-250](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/250.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

#### F-044 · Server-side code execution (routes/b2bOrder.ts:23)

**Severity:** 🟠 High _(raw Critical)_  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/b2bOrder.ts:23`

**Issue:** `b2bOrder()` passes attacker-controlled `body.orderLinesData` into `vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, { timeout: 2000 })` using the `notevil` sandbox. `notevil` has known escape/DoS gaps; an authenticated B2B user POSTs to /b2b/v2/orders with a crafted expression to break out of the sandbox for RCE, or an infinite-loop payload to exhaust the event loop (the code itself detects the timeout as rceOccupyChallenge).

Server-side eval of request data is remote code execution. Potential remote code execution / sandbox escape and reliable worker DoS on the order-processing path.

**Root cause:** User-supplied data reaches a server-side code-execution sink (`eval`, sandbox primitives, deserialization, prototype-pollution gadgets) and breaks out into arbitrary native execution.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `body.orderLinesData` reaches an eval sandbox at `b2bOrder.ts:23` with only a 2s timeout as containment.

```typescript
// routes/b2bOrder.ts:23
        const sandbox = { safeEval, orderLinesData }
        vm.createContext(sandbox)
        vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, { timeout: 2000 })
        res.json({ cid: body.cid, orderNo: uniqueOrderNumber(), paymentDue: dateTwoWeeksFromNow() })
      } catch (err) {
```

**Fix:** Replace runtime code generation (eval/Function/template render) with a data-only execution path → ◕ [M-047](#m-047) — Remove server-side evaluation of untrusted input (`b2bOrder.ts:23`)

**Classification:** Code Execution via Unsafe Deserialization or Eval · [CWE-94](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/94.html) · [OWASP A08:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A08_2021/)

#### F-019 · NoSQL Injection (routes/showProductReviews.ts:36)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/showProductReviews.ts:36`

**Issue:** `showProductReviews()` builds a MongoDB `$where` clause by concatenating `req.params.id` into server-side JavaScript: `reviewsCollection.find({ $where: 'this.product == ' + id })`. When the noSqlCommandChallenge is enabled the id is only truncated to 40 chars (not numeric-coerced), so an attacker sends GET /rest/products/:id/reviews with id=`0;while(true){}` to hang the JS engine (NoSQL DoS) or id=`0;return true` to return every review document regardless of product.

Server-side JS evaluation in the Mongo engine enabling data-wide reads and query-thread stalls.

**Root cause:** User input flows into a server-side interpreter (SQL, NoSQL, XML, YAML, LDAP, OS shell) without parameterization or schema validation.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `req.params.id` is concatenated into a Mongo \$where JavaScript predicate at `showProductReviews.ts:36` without coercion when the challenge path is active.

```typescript
// routes/showProductReviews.ts:36
    const t0 = new Date().getTime()

    db.reviewsCollection.find({ $where: 'this.product == ' + id }).then((reviews: Review[]) => {
      const t1 = new Date().getTime()
      challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.noSqlCommandChallenge, () => { return (t1 - t0) > 2000 })
```

**Fix:** Replace string concatenation in query operators with parameter binding → ◕ [M-024](#m-024) — Use parameterized database queries (`showProductReviews.ts:36`)

**Classification:** Injection · [CWE-943](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/943.html) · [OWASP A03:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A03_2021/)

<a id="t-023"></a><a id="f-023"></a>
#### F-023 · JWT session token stored in localStorage readable (request.interceptor.ts:16)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/Services/request.interceptor.ts:16`

**Issue:** The session JWT is written to localStorage on every login path (`login.component.ts:101`, `oauth.component.ts:51`, `payment.component.ts:232`) and read back to build the `Authorization: Bearer` header in `request.interceptor.ts`:16. localStorage is readable and writable by any JavaScript executing in the origin, so the token has no isolation from XSS: any of the injection sinks in this component (🔴 [F-015](#f-015)/004/005) can exfiltrate it with a single `localStorage.getItem('token')`.

The user's email is likewise stored (`login.component.ts:135`) and forwarded in an `X-User-Email` header (`request.interceptor.ts:23`). Any XSS or local-device access yields the full session token, enabling silent account takeover.

**Root cause:** Attacker-controlled content is rendered in the victim's browser without sanitization; combined with session tokens held in JavaScript-readable storage, any payload yields immediate account takeover.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The bearer JWT is persisted in localStorage and a flag-less cookie, both fully readable by page scripts, and re-read by the HTTP interceptor.

**Fix:** ◑ [M-028](#m-028) — Store session tokens in HttpOnly, Secure cookies (`request.interceptor.ts:16`)

**Classification:** Insecure Client-Side Storage · [CWE-922](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/922.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

Password and totpSecret are masked with asterisks (lines 26-27) but their length is still leaked. Whole-directory user enumeration (emails, roles, IPs) enabling targeted phishing and privilege-focused attacks.

```typescript
// models/card.ts:38
      },
      fullName: DataTypes.STRING,
      cardNum: {
        type: DataTypes.INTEGER,
        validate: {
```

<a id="t-014"></a><a id="f-014"></a>
#### F-014 · Open redirect (routes/redirect.ts:19)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/redirect.ts:19`

**Issue:** `performRedirect()` takes the attacker-controlled `to` query parameter and passes it to `security.isRedirectAllowed()`, which validates with url.includes(allowedUrl) - a substring test, not a prefix/host test. An anonymous attacker crafts /redirect?to=https://evil.example/#https://github.com/juice-shop/juice-shop: the URL contains an allowlisted string so isRedirectAllowed returns true, and res.redirect(toUrl) at line 19 sends the victim's browser to the attacker-controlled host.

This enables phishing and OAuth/token-forwarding chains under the trusted application origin. Victims are redirected to attacker-chosen sites while trusting the Juice Shop origin, enabling credential phishing and malware delivery.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `redirect.ts:19` calls res.redirect(toUrl) with the raw `to` value after only the `includes()`-based check, so any URL that embeds an allowlisted substring passes.

```typescript
// routes/redirect.ts:19
      challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.redirectCryptoCurrencyChallenge, () => { return toUrl === 'https://explorer.dash.org/address/Xr556RzuwX6hg5EGpkybbv5RanJoZN17kW' || toUrl === 'https://blockchain.info/address/1AbKfgvw9psQ41NbLi8kufDQTezwG8DRZm' || toUrl === 'https://etherscan.io/address/0x0f933ab9fcaaa782d0279c300d73750e1311eae6' })
      challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.redirectChallenge, () => { return isUnintendedRedirect(toUrl) })
      res.redirect(toUrl)
    } else {
      res.status(406)
```

**Fix:** ◕ [M-019](#m-019) — Validate redirect targets against an allowlist (`redirect.ts:19`)

**Classification:** Open Redirect · [CWE-601](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/601.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-015"></a><a id="f-015"></a>
#### F-015 · Cross-Site Scripting (search-result.component.ts:143)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts:143`

**Instances (3):** `frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts:143`, `frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts:110`, `frontend/src/app/last-login-ip/last-login-ip.component.ts:39`

**Issue:** `SearchResultComponent.filterTable()` takes the `q` query-string parameter and passes it through `this.sanitizer.bypassSecurityTrustHtml(queryParam)` (`search-result.component.ts:143`), storing the result in `searchValue`, which the template renders with `<span id="searchValue" [innerHTML]="searchValue">` (`search-result.component.html:11`). bypassSecurityTrustHtml explicitly disables Angular's built-in output encoding, so an attacker who sends a victim a link such as `/#/search?q=<img src=x onerror=alert(document.cookie)>` executes arbitrary JavaScript in the victim's origin.

Because the session JWT lives in localStorage (see 🟠 [F-023](#f-023)), the payload can read and exfiltrate the token. Arbitrary script execution in the victim's session, enabling JWT theft from localStorage and full account takeover.

**Root cause:** Attacker-controlled content is rendered in the victim's browser without sanitization; combined with session tokens held in JavaScript-readable storage, any payload yields immediate account takeover.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The reflected `q` parameter is wrapped in bypassSecurityTrustHtml and rendered through [innerHTML], disabling Angular's default escaping.

```typescript
// frontend/src/app/search-result/search-result.component.ts:143
      }) // vuln-code-snippet hide-end
      this.dataSource.filter = queryParam.toLowerCase()
      this.searchValue = this.sanitizer.bypassSecurityTrustHtml(queryParam) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line localXssChallenge xssBonusChallenge
      if (this.gridDataSourceSubscription) {
        this.gridDataSourceSubscription.unsubscribe()
```

**Fix:** Output-encode untrusted strings at every sink and remove all `bypassSecurityTrustHtml` calls → ◕ [M-020](#m-020) — Encode output instead of bypassing the framework sanitizer (`search-result.component.ts:143`)

**Classification:** Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) · [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [OWASP A03:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A03_2021/)

### 🟡 Medium (15)

<a id="t-046"></a><a id="f-046"></a>
#### F-046 · Hardcoded cookie signing secret 'kekse' (server.ts:289)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium - secret committed to the public source repo - extractable on clone, no prior access needed  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:289`

**Issue:** cookieParser is initialised with the literal secret 'kekse'. Because the secret is committed to source, an attacker who knows it (trivially, from this public repo) can forge or tamper with any signed cookie the application trusts and defeat signature validation on cookie-carried state.

Forgery and tampering of signed cookies, undermining any integrity assumption placed on cookie values.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The cookie-parser signing secret is the hardcoded literal 'kekse' at `server.ts`:289.

**Fix:** Move the credential out of source control into a secret store and rotate it → ◑ [M-049](#m-049) — Move secrets to a managed secret store (`server.ts:289`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-057"></a><a id="f-057"></a>
#### F-057 · Security answers keyed with a hardcoded static (models/securityAnswer.ts:45)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium - secret committed to the public source repo - extractable on clone, no prior access needed  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - SQLite3/Sequelize Data Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/securityAnswer.ts:45`

**Issue:** The SecurityAnswer model's `answer` setter stores `security.hmac(answer)`, where `security.hmac` (`lib/insecurity.ts:42`) is `crypto.createHmac('sha256', 'pa4qacea4VK9t9nGv7yZtwmj')` - a single application-wide key committed to the source tree. Because the key is public and the transform is deterministic and unsalted, an attacker who reads the SecurityAnswers table can precompute HMACs of a dictionary of common answers to recover secret-question responses offline, and can trivially see when two users share the same answer (identical digests).

Offline dictionary recovery and cross-user correlation of security answers, enabling account-recovery abuse.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The answer `set()` hook applies `security.hmac`, which keys HMAC-SHA256 with the literal string 'pa4qacea4VK9t9nGv7yZtwmj' hardcoded in `insecurity.ts`, giving a deterministic unsalted digest.

**Fix:** Move the credential out of source control into a secret store and rotate it → ◑ [M-058](#m-058) — Move secrets to a managed secret store (`securityAnswer.ts:45`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-047"></a><a id="f-047"></a>
#### F-047 · Docker base image on floating tag, not digest

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `Dockerfile:1`

**Issue:** `Dockerfile:1` builds the installer stage from `FROM node:24` and the runtime stage from `gcr.io/distroless/nodejs24-debian13` (:22) - both mutable tags with no `@sha256:` digest pin. The content behind these tags changes over time and could be repointed or poisoned upstream, so two builds of the same commit are not guaranteed to produce byte-identical layers, and a compromised registry entry would flow straight into the published `bkimminich/juice-shop` image.

A repointed or compromised base-image tag introduces unreviewed content into every published Juice Shop image.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `Dockerfile:1` and `:22` reference base images by mutable tag with no digest, breaking build reproducibility and provenance.

**Fix:** ◑ [M-050](#m-050) — Pin third-party dependencies to immutable versions (`Dockerfile:1`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-048"></a><a id="f-048"></a>
#### F-048 · Legacy Dependabot v1 config is not processed (.dependabot/config.yml:1)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.dependabot/config.yml:1`

**Issue:** `.dependabot/config.yml:1` uses the deprecated Dependabot v1 schema (`version: 1`, `update_configs:`, `update_schedule: live`) served by the retired `dependabot.com` integration. GitHub-native Dependabot reads only `.github/dependabot.yml` with `version: 2`, which is absent from the repo.

Dependency updates are not actually automated, so known-vulnerable packages accumulate undetected in builds and releases.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `.dependabot/config.yml:1` is the retired v1 format; no `.github/dependabot.yml` v2 exists, so GitHub-native Dependabot never runs.

**Fix:** Replace the unmaintained dependency with a maintained equivalent or fork it under ownership → ◑ [M-051](#m-051) — Pin the container base image to an immutable digest (`config.yml:1`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-1104](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1104.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-050"></a><a id="f-050"></a>
#### F-050 · Wildcard CORS and missing CSP/HSTS response headers (server.ts:183)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:183`

**Issue:** The app enables CORS globally with a bare `app.use(cors())` (`server.ts:182-183`), reflecting Access-Control-Allow-Origin for all origins, and helmet is limited to `noSniff()` and `frameguard()` (`server.ts:186-188`) with Content-Security-Policy and HSTS explicitly absent (the xssFilter line is commented out at 188). The permissive cross-origin policy lets any website read responses from browser sessions, and the missing CSP removes the primary defence against the persistent XSS this API stores.

Cross-origin data exposure to any site and no CSP backstop against stored/DOM XSS delivered through the API.

**Root cause:** A permissive CORS policy plus missing anti-CSRF tokens let any external page issue authenticated state-changing requests in the victim's session.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `server.ts:183` applies unrestricted `cors()`; `server.ts:186-188` configures only noSniff and frameguard, with no CSP or HSTS.

**Fix:** Replace the wildcard CORS origin with an explicit allow-list → ◑ [M-053](#m-053) — Restrict CORS to known origins and add CSP + HSTS headers (`server.ts:183`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-942](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/942.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-051"></a><a id="f-051"></a>
#### F-051 · Content-Type-only upload filter on /rest/memories (server.ts:701)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:701`

**Issue:** The uploadToDisk multer instance (`server.ts:698-711`) decides validity solely from `file.mimetype`, which is derived from the client-supplied Content-Type header, against mimeTypeMap (png/jpg/jpeg). Unlike profileImageFileUpload, this route (/rest/memories) performs NO magic-byte verification.

Storage of arbitrary attacker content in a public directory via a trivially spoofed header.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The destination callback at `server.ts:701` validates only `mimeTypeMap[file.mimetype]` (the spoofable Content-Type header) with no `fileType.fromBuffer` magic-byte check on this route.

**Fix:** Validate uploaded file type, size, and storage path; never execute uploaded content → ◑ [M-054](#m-054) — Verify uploaded image bytes with magic-byte detection on /rest/memories, not the (`server.ts:701`)

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-434](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/434.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-052"></a><a id="f-052"></a>
#### F-052 · Container image signing (update-news-www.yml:1)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium - elevated as an attack-chain keystone (individual baseline: High)  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/update-news-www.yml:1`

**Instances (16):** `.github/workflows/update-news-www.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/rebase.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/lock.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/update-challenges-ebook.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/update-news-www-legacy.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/release.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/zap_scan.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:1` … (+8 more)

**Issue:** Container image signing via cosign or attest-build-provenance - .github/workflows/update-news-www.yml:1. Unsigned container images cannot be verified for provenance - any registry intermediary could substitute them.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified

<a id="t-053"></a><a id="f-053"></a>

<a id="t-054"></a><a id="f-054"></a>
#### F-054 · Unauthenticated admin application-configuration endpoint (server.ts:607)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Express\.js REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:607`

**Issue:** GET /rest/admin/application-configuration is registered with no authorization middleware in front of `retrieveAppConfiguration()`. The handler returns the whole config object (minus only `chatBot.llmApiUrl`). Anonymous disclosure of internal application configuration under an /rest/admin path.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `server.ts:607` wires the admin config handler directly with no `isAuthorized()` guard.

**Fix:** ◑ [M-055](#m-055) — Require authentication on every exposed endpoint (`server.ts:607`)
